<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shuttle_disasters">Shuttle disasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Shuttle disasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">Space Shuttle Challenger disaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">Space Shuttle Columbia disaster</a></div>
<p>On January 28, 1986, <i>Challenger</i> disintegrated 73 seconds after launch due to the failure of the right SRB, killing all seven astronauts on board. The disaster was caused by low-temperature impairment of an O-ring, a mission critical seal used between segments of the SRB casing. Failure of the O-ring allowed hot combustion gases to escape from between the booster sections and burn through the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">external tank</a>, causing it to explode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Repeated warnings from design engineers voicing concerns about the lack of evidence of the O-rings' safety when the temperature was below 53 °F (12 °C) had been ignored by NASA managers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 1, 2003, <i>Columbia</i> disintegrated during re-entry, killing its crew of seven, because of damage to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reinforced_carbon-carbon" title="Reinforced carbon-carbon">carbon-carbon</a> leading edge of the wing caused during launch. Ground control engineers had made three separate requests for high-resolution images taken by the Department of Defense that would have provided an understanding of the extent of the damage, while NASA's chief <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space Shuttle thermal protection system">thermal protection system</a> (TPS) engineer requested that astronauts on board <i>Columbia</i> be allowed to leave the vehicle to inspect the damage. NASA managers intervened to stop the Department of Defense's assistance and refused the request for the spacewalk,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and thus the feasibility of scenarios for astronaut repair or rescue by <i>Atlantis</i> were not considered by NASA management at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_retirement" title="Space Shuttle retirement">Space Shuttle retirement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="908" data-file-width="1639" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png/330px-Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png/495px-Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png/660px-Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantis_welcome_home_ceremony_outside_the_OPF_July_22.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Atlantis</i> orbiter's final welcome home, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>NASA retired the Space Shuttle in 2011, after 30 years of service. The Shuttle was originally conceived of and presented to the public as a "Space Truck", which would, among other things, be used to build a United States space station in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_earth_orbit" title="Low earth orbit">low earth orbit</a> in the early 1990s. When the US space station evolved into the International Space Station project, which suffered from long delays and design changes before it could be completed, the retirement of the Space Shuttle was delayed several times until 2011, serving at least 15 years longer than originally planned. <i>Discovery</i> was the first of NASA's three remaining operational Space Shuttles to be retired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>The final Space Shuttle mission was originally scheduled for late 2010, but the program was later extended to July 2011 when Michael Suffredini of the ISS program said that one additional trip was needed in 2011 to deliver parts to the International Space Station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The Shuttle's final mission consisted of just four astronauts—Christopher Ferguson (Commander), Douglas Hurley (Pilot), Sandra Magnus (Mission Specialist 1), and Rex Walheim (Mission Specialist 2);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> they conducted the 135th and last space Shuttle mission on board <i>Atlantis</i>, which launched on July 8, 2011, and landed safely at the Kennedy Space Center on July 21, 2011, at 5:57 AM EDT (09:57 UTC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution_of_orbiters_and_other_hardware">Distribution of orbiters and other hardware</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Distribution of orbiters and other hardware">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2168" data-file-width="1740" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png/130px-Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png/195px-Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png/260px-Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Program_Commemorative_Patch.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Program" title="Space Shuttle Program">Space Shuttle Program</a> commemorative patch</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>NASA announced it would transfer orbiters to education institutions or museums at the conclusion of the Space Shuttle program. Each museum or institution is responsible for covering the <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$28.8 million</span> cost of preparing and transporting each vehicle for display. Twenty museums from across the country submitted proposals for receiving one of the retired orbiters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retired_shuttle_display_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-retired_shuttle_display-104">[104]</a></sup> NASA also made <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space Shuttle thermal protection system">Space Shuttle thermal protection system</a> tiles available to schools and universities for less than US$25 each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiles_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-tiles-105">[105]</a></sup> About 7,000 tiles were available on a <a href="/wiki/First-come,_first-served" title="First-come, first-served">first-come, first-served</a> basis, limited to one per institution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiles_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-tiles-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orbiters_On_Display">Orbiters On Display</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Orbiters On Display">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On April 12, 2011, NASA announced selection of locations for the remaining Shuttle orbiters:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_New_Homes_for_Orbiters_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_New_Homes_for_Orbiters-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intrepid_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-intrepid-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><i>Atlantis</i> is on display at the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">Cape Canaveral</a>, Florida. It was delivered to the Visitor Complex on November 2, 2012.</li>
<li><i>Discovery</i> was delivered to the <a href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy_Center" title="Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center">Udvar-Hazy Center</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">National Air and Space Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chantilly,_Virginia" title="Chantilly, Virginia">Chantilly, Virginia</a>, near Washington, D.C. on April 19, 2012. On April 17, 2012, <i>Discovery</i> was flown atop a 747 Shuttle Carrier Aircraft escorted by a NASA T-38 Talon chase aircraft in a final farewell flight. The 747 and <i>Discovery</i> flew over Washington, D.C. and the metropolitan area around 10 am and arrived at Dulles around 11 am. The flyover and landing were widely covered on national news media.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG/220px-Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG/330px-Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG/440px-Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Endeavor_Touchdown_at_LAX.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Endeavour</i> at Los Angeles International Airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><i>Endeavour</i> was delivered to the <a href="/wiki/California_Science_Center" title="California Science Center">California Science Center</a> in Los Angeles, California on October 14, 2012. It arrived at Los Angeles International Airport on September 21, 2012, concluding a two-day, cross country journey atop the Shuttle Carrier Aircraft after stops at Ellington Field in Houston, Biggs Army Airfield in El Paso and the Dryden Flight Research Facility at Edwards Air Force Base, California.</li>
<li><i>Enterprise</i> (atmospheric test orbiter) was on display at the National Air and Space Museum's Udvar-Hazy Center but was moved to New York City's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intrepid_Sea-Air-Space_Museum" title="Intrepid Sea-Air-Space Museum">Intrepid Sea-Air-Space Museum</a> in mid-2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shuttle_sale_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-shuttle_sale-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>In August 2011, the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Office_of_Inspector_General" title="NASA Office of Inspector General">NASA Office of Inspector General</a> (OIG) published a "Review of NASA's Selection of Display Locations for the Space Shuttle Orbiters"; the review had four main findings:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oigreview_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-oigreview-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"NASA's decisions regarding Orbiter placement were the result of an Agency-created process that emphasized above all other considerations locating the Orbiters in places where the most people would have the opportunity to view them";</li>
<li>"the Team made several errors during its evaluation process, including one that would have resulted in a numerical 'tie' among the Intrepid, the Kennedy Visitor Complex, and the National Museum of the U.S. Air Force (Air Force Museum) in Dayton, Ohio";</li>
<li>there is "no evidence that the Team’s recommendation or the Administrator's decision were tainted by political influence or any other improper consideration";</li>
<li>"some of the choices NASA made during the selection process – specifically, its decision to manage aspects of the selection as if it were a competitive procurement and to delay announcement of its placement decisions until April 2011 (more than 2 years after it first solicited information from interested entities)—may intensify challenges to the Agency and the selectees as they work to complete the process of placing the Orbiters in their new homes."</li>
</ul>
<p>The NASA OIG had three recommendations, saying NASA should:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oigreview_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-oigreview-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"expeditiously review recipients' financial, logistical, and curatorial display plans to ensure they are feasible and consistent with the Agency's educational goals and processing and delivery schedules";</li>
<li>"ensure that recipient payments are closely coordinated with processing schedules, do not impede NASA's ability to efficiently prepare the Orbiters for museum display, and provide sufficient funds in advance of the work to be performed; and"</li>
<li>"work closely with the recipient organizations to minimize the possibility of delays in the delivery schedule that could increase the Agency's costs or impact other NASA missions and priorities."</li>
</ul>
<p>In September 2011, the CEO and two board members of Seattle's Museum of Flight met with NASA Administrator <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bolden" title="Charles Bolden">Charles Bolden</a>, pointing out "significant errors in deciding where to put its four retiring Space Shuttles"; the errors alleged include inaccurate information on Museum of Flight's attendance and international visitor statistics, as well as the readiness of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intrepid_Sea-Air-Space_Museum" title="Intrepid Sea-Air-Space Museum">Intrepid Sea-Air-Space Museum</a>'s exhibit site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orbiter_Replicas_On_Display">Orbiter Replicas On Display</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Orbiter Replicas On Display">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Independence" title="Space Shuttle Independence"><i>Independence</i></a>, formerly known as <i>Explorer</i>, is a full-scale, high-fidelity replica of the Space Shuttle. It was built by <a href="/wiki/Guard-Lee" title="Guard-Lee">Guard-Lee</a> in <a href="/wiki/Apopka,_Florida" title="Apopka, Florida">Apopka, Florida</a>, installed at <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex</a> in 1993, and moved to <a href="/wiki/Space_Center_Houston" title="Space Center Houston">Space Center Houston</a> in 2012. It was built using schematics, blueprints and archival documents provided by NASA and by shuttle contractors such as <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_International" title="Rockwell International">Rockwell International</a>. While many of the features on the replica are simulated, some parts, including the landing gear's <a href="/wiki/Michelin" title="Michelin">Michelin</a> tires, have been used in the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle program</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collect20120524_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-collect20120524-110">[110]</a></sup> The model is on display, mounted on top of the original <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Carrier_Aircraft" title="Shuttle Carrier Aircraft">Shuttle Carrier Aircraft</a> (NASA 905) outside of the Visitors' Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insider20140815_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-insider20140815-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Pathfinder" title="Space Shuttle Pathfinder"><i>Pathfinder</i></a> (honorary <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Vehicle_Designation" title="Orbiter Vehicle Designation">Orbiter Vehicle Designation</a>: OV-098) is a Space Shuttle test simulator made of <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wood" title="Wood">wood</a>. Constructed by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> in 1977 as an unnamed <a href="/wiki/Test_article" title="Test article">test article</a>, it was purchased in the early 1980s by the America-Japan Society, Inc. which had it refurbished, named it, and placed it on display in the Great Space Shuttle Exhibition in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>. The mockup was later returned to the United States and placed on permanent display at the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Space_%26_Rocket_Center" title="U.S. Space &amp; Rocket Center">U.S. Space &amp; Rocket Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville, Alabama</a>, in May 1988.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware_On_Display">Hardware On Display</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hardware On Display">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Flight and mid-deck training hardware will be taken from the <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">Johnson Space Center</a> and will go to the National Air and Space Museum and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_U.S._Air_Force" title="National Museum of the U.S. Air Force">National Museum of the U.S. Air Force</a>. The full fuselage mockup, which includes the payload bay and aft section but no wings, is to go to the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Flight" title="Museum of Flight">Museum of Flight</a> in Seattle. Mission Simulation and Training Facility's fixed simulator will go to the <a href="/wiki/Adler_Planetarium" title="Adler Planetarium">Adler Planetarium</a> in Chicago, and the motion simulator will go to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M" title="Texas A&amp;M">Texas A&amp;M</a> Aerospace Engineering Department in College Station, Texas. Other simulators used in Shuttle astronaut training will go to the <a href="/wiki/Wings_of_Dreams_Aviation_Museum" title="Wings of Dreams Aviation Museum">Wings of Dreams Aviation Museum</a> in Starke, Florida and the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Air_and_Space_Center" title="Virginia Air and Space Center">Virginia Air and Space Center</a> in Hampton, Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retired_shuttle_display_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-retired_shuttle_display-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Shuttle_successors_and_legacy">Space Shuttle successors and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Space Shuttle successors and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_retirement" title="Space Shuttle retirement">Space Shuttle retirement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="627" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg/220px-Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg/330px-Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg/440px-Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Critical-ionization-velocity.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
STS conducted numerous experiments in space, such as this ionization experiment</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg/220px-Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg/330px-Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg/440px-Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Robot_Camera_Retrieval_-_GPN-2000-001089.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sprint cameras, tested by the Shuttle, may be used on ISS and other missions</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Until another US manned spacecraft is ready, crews will travel to and from the International Space Station (ISS) exclusively aboard the Russian <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(spacecraft)" title="Soyuz (spacecraft)">Soyuz</a> spacecraft.</p>
<p>A planned successor to STS was the "Shuttle II", during the 1980s and 1990s, and later the Constellation program during the 2004–2010 period. CSTS was a proposal to continue to operate STS commercially, after NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coppinger_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-coppinger-112">[112]</a></sup> In September 2011, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> announced the selection of the design for the new <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> that is planned to launch the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" title="Orion spacecraft">Orion spacecraft</a> and other hardware to missions beyond low earth-orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Heavy-lift_Rocket_Will_Take_Humans_Far_Beyond_Earth_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Heavy-lift_Rocket_Will_Take_Humans_Far_Beyond_Earth-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_Briefing_on_Deep_Space_Launch_System_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_Briefing_on_Deep_Space_Launch_System-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_.26_Cosmos_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Space_.26_Cosmos-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">Commercial Orbital Transportation Services</a> program began in 2006 with the purpose of creating commercially operated unmanned cargo vehicles to service the ISS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">Commercial Crew Development</a> (CCDev) program was started in 2010 to create commercially operated manned spacecraft capable of delivering at least four crew members to the ISS, to stay docked for 180 days, and then return them back to Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> These spacecraft were to become operational in the 2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Space Shuttles have been features of fiction and nonfiction, from children's movies to documentaries. Early examples include the 1979 <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond</a></i> film, <i><a href="/wiki/Moonraker_(film)" title="Moonraker (film)">Moonraker</a></i>, the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a> videogame <i>Space Shuttle: A Journey into Space</i> (1982) and <a href="/wiki/G._Harry_Stine" title="G. Harry Stine">G. Harry Stine</a>'s 1981 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Down" title="Shuttle Down">Shuttle Down</a></i>. In the 1986 film <i><a href="/wiki/SpaceCamp" title="SpaceCamp">SpaceCamp</a></i>, <i>Atlantis</i> accidentally launched into space with a group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Space_Camp" title="U.S. Space Camp">U.S. Space Camp</a> participants as its crew. The 1998 film <i><a href="/wiki/Armageddon_(1998_film)" title="Armageddon (1998 film)">Armageddon</a></i> portrayed a combined crew of offshore oil rig workers and US military staff who pilot two modified Shuttles to avert the destruction of Earth by an asteroid. Retired American test pilots visited a Russian satellite in the 2000 <a href="/wiki/Clint_Eastwood" title="Clint Eastwood">Clint Eastwood</a> adventure film <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Cowboys" title="Space Cowboys">Space Cowboys</a></i>. In the 2003 film <i>The Core,</i> the <i>Endeavour</i>'s landing is disrupted by the Earth's magnetic core, and its crew is selected to pilot the vehicle designed to restart the core. The 2004 Bollywood movie <i><a href="/wiki/Swades" title="Swades">Swades</a></i>, where a Space Shuttle was used to launch a special rainfall monitoring satellite, was filmed at Kennedy Space Center in the year following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_disaster" title="Columbia disaster">Columbia disaster</a> that had taken the life of Indian-American astronaut <a href="/wiki/Kalpana_Chawla" title="Kalpana Chawla">KC Chawla</a>.</p>
<p>On television, the 1996 drama <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cape_(1996_TV_series)" title="The Cape (1996 TV series)">The Cape</a></i> portrayed the lives of a group of NASA astronauts as they prepared for and flew Shuttle missions. <i><a href="/wiki/Odyssey_5" title="Odyssey 5">Odyssey 5</a></i> was a short lived sci-fi series that featured the crew of a Space Shuttle as the last survivors of a disaster that destroyed Earth. The 1997- 2007 sci-fi series <i>Stargate SG-1</i> had a shuttle rescue written into an episode.</p>
<p>The 2013 film <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(2013_film)" title="Gravity (2013 film)">Gravity</a></i> features the fictional Space Shuttle <i>Explorer</i> during STS-157, whose crew are killed or left stranded after it is destroyed by a shower of high speed orbital debris.</p>
<p>The 2017 <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lego_Batman_Movie" title="The Lego Batman Movie">The Lego Batman Movie</a></i> features an hybrid between the <a href="/wiki/Batmobile" title="Batmobile">Batmobile</a> and a Space Shuttle, named "the Bat Space Shuttle" by <a href="/wiki/Dick_Grayson" title="Dick Grayson">Dick Grayson</a>. It's clearly based on the <a href="/wiki/Lego_City" title="Lego City">Lego City</a> set 3367 ("Space Shuttle"), but it's black and weapon-equipped.</p>
<p><br/></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_320c.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="244" data-file-width="298" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/69/Space_Shuttle_320c.jpg/220px-Space_Shuttle_320c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/69/Space_Shuttle_320c.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_320c.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A United States Space Shuttle stamp</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Space Shuttle has also been the subject of toys and models; for example, a large <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> Space Shuttle model was constructed by visitors at Kennedy Space Center,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and smaller models have been sold commercially as a standard "LegoLand" set. A 1980 pinball machine <i>Space Shuttle</i> was produced by <a href="/wiki/Zaccaria_(company)" title="Zaccaria (company)">Zaccaria</a> and a 1984 pinball machine <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_(pinball)" title="Space Shuttle (pinball)">Space Shuttle: Pinball Adventure</a></i> was produced by <a href="/wiki/WMS_Industries" title="WMS Industries">Williams</a> and features a plastic Space Shuttle model among other artwork of astronauts on the play field. The Space Shuttle also appears in a number of <a href="/wiki/Amateur_flight_simulation" title="Amateur flight simulation">flight simulator</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_flight_simulator_game" title="Space flight simulator game">space flight simulator games</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Space_Simulator" title="Microsoft Space Simulator">Microsoft Space Simulator</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Orbiter_(simulator)" title="Orbiter (simulator)">Orbiter</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/FlightGear" title="FlightGear">FlightGear</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X-Plane_(simulator)" title="X-Plane (simulator)">X-Plane</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Mission_2007" title="Space Shuttle Mission 2007">Space Shuttle Mission 2007</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Transformers_(toy_line)" title="Transformers (toy line)">Transformers toys</a> were modeled after the Space Shuttle.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_postage_commemorations">US postage commemorations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: US postage commemorations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/U.S._space_exploration_history_on_U.S._stamps#Space_Shuttle_Issues" title="U.S. space exploration history on U.S. stamps">U.S. space exploration history on U.S. stamps § Space Shuttle Issues</a></div>
<p>The U.S. Postal Service has released several postage issues that depict the Space Shuttle. The first such stamps were issued in 1981, and are on display at the <a href="/wiki/National_Postal_Museum" title="National Postal Museum">National Postal Museum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Similar_spacecraft">Similar spacecraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Similar spacecraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boeing_X-20_Dyna-Soar" title="Boeing X-20 Dyna-Soar">Boeing X-20 Dyna-Soar</a> (1957–1963)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buran_programme" title="Buran programme">Buran</a>, Soviet Space shuttle program (1974–1992)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_orbital_launch_systems" title="Comparison of orbital launch systems">Comparison of orbital launch systems</a></li>

<div style="padding:0px;">
<table class="navbox-columns-table" style="border-spacing: 0px; text-align:left;width:100%;">
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="1" style="font-weight:bold;text-align: left;">United States <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle program</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Space_Shuttle_orbiters" title="List of Space Shuttle orbiters">list</a>)</td>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="1" style="border-left:2px solid #fdfdfd;font-weight:bold;text-align: left;">Soviet/Russian <a href="/wiki/Buran_programme" title="Buran programme">Buran programme</a></td>
</tr>
<tr style="vertical-align:top;">
<td class="navbox-list" style="padding:0px;;;;width:10em;">
<div>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Pathfinder" title="Space Shuttle Pathfinder">Pathfinder</a></i> <small>(OV-098, ground tests)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">Challenger</a></i> <small>(OV-099, <b><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">destroyed in 1986</a></b>)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Enterprise" title="Space Shuttle Enterprise">Enterprise</a></i> <small>(OV-101, atmospheric tests, retired in 1979)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">Columbia</a></i> <small>(OV-102, <b><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">destroyed in 2003</a></b>)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">Discovery</a></i> <small>(OV-103, retired in 2011)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">Atlantis</a></i> <small>(OV-104, retired in 2011)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">Endeavour</a></i> <small>(OV-105, retired in 2011)</small></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
<td class="navbox-list" style="border-left:2px solid #fdfdfd;padding:0px;;;;width:10em;">
<div>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/OK-GLI" title="OK-GLI">OK-GLI</a></i> <small>(Buran Analog BST-02, aerotester)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Buran_(spacecraft)" title="Buran (spacecraft)">Buran</a></i> <small>(Shuttle 1.01, destroyed in 2002)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ptichka" title="Ptichka">Ptichka</a></i> <small>(Shuttle 1.02, 95–97% completed)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/2.01_(Buran-class_spacecraft)" title="2.01 (Buran-class spacecraft)">Baikal</a></i> <small>(Shuttle 2.01, incomplete)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/2.02_(Buran-class_spacecraft)" title="2.02 (Buran-class spacecraft)">2.02</a></i> <small>(partially dismantled)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/2.03_(Buran-class_spacecraft)" title="2.03 (Buran-class spacecraft)">2.03</a></i> <small>(dismantled)</small></li>
</ul>
</div>
